To determine if 9103 is a prime number, we can apply the same steps as mentioned before:

1.  Firstly, we check if 9103 is divisible by any prime numbers less than its square root, rounded up to the nearest whole number. The square root of 9103 is approximately 95.43, so we only need to check for divisibility by prime numbers up to 95.

2.  We start by checking if 9103 is divisible by 2. Since it is an odd number, it is not divisible by 2.

3.  Next, we check divisibility by 3. The sum of the digits in 9103 is 9 + 1 + 0 + 3 = 13, which is not divisible by 3. Hence, 9103 is not divisible by 3.

4.  Then, we check divisibility by 5. Since the last digit of 9103 is 3, which is not 0 or 5, it is not divisible by 5.

5.  Moving on, we check divisibility by 7. To do this, we can use the technique of subtracting multiples of 7 from 9103. By subtracting 7 from 9103 repeatedly until we get a number less than 100, we find that 9103 - 7 × 1300 = 43. Since 43 is not divisible by 7, 9103 is not divisible by 7.

6.  Finally, we check divisibility by 11. If the difference between the sum of the alternating digits (from left to right) and the sum of the remaining digits is divisible by 11, then the number is divisible by 11. In this case, 9 - (1 + 0 + 3) = 5, which is not divisible by 11. Therefore, 9103 is not divisible by 11.

Since 9103 is not divisible by any prime numbers less than its square root, it follows that 9103 is a prime number.

Therefore, the answer is "Yes, 9103 is a prime number."

To determine if 9293 is a composite number, we need to check if it has any factors other than 1 and itself. We can do this by dividing 9293 by all numbers from 2 to the square root of 9293, and if any of these divisions result in a whole number, then 9293 is a composite number.

However, calculating all these divisions manually might take some time. So, let's write a Python code to check if 9293 is a composite number:

```python
import math

def is_composite(n):
    if n < 2:
        return False
    for i in range(2, int(math.sqrt(n)) + 1):
        if n % i == 0:
            return True
    return False

number = 9293

if is_composite(number):
    print("Yes, 9293 is a composite number.")
else:
    print("No, 9293 is not a composite number.")
```

After running this code, we find that 9293 is not a composite number.

To determine if 7237 is a composite number, we need to check if it is divisible by any number other than 1 and itself.

Step 1: We can start by checking if it is divisible by 2. 
The number 7237 is not divisible by 2 because it does not end in an even digit (0, 2, 4, 6, or 8).

Step 2: Next, we can check if it is divisible by 3. To do this, we add up its digits and check if the sum is divisible by 3.
7 + 2 + 3 + 7 = 19
The sum 19 is not divisible by 3, so 7237 is not divisible by 3.

Step 3: We can also check if it is divisible by 5. If the last digit of a number is either 0 or 5, then the number is divisible by 5.
The last digit of 7237 is 7, so it is not divisible by 5.

Step 4: Now, let's check if it is divisible by 7 using the "divisibility by 7" rule.
Taking twice the units digit of 7237, we get 7 * 2 = 14.
Subtracting 14 from the remaining digits (723) gives us 709.
709 is not divisible by 7, so 7237 is not divisible by 7.

Step 5: Finally, we check if it is divisible by 11.
The sum of odd-placed digits (7 + 3) is 10, and the sum of even-placed digits (2 + 7) is 9.
The difference between 10 and 9 is 1, which is neither 0 nor divisible by 11. Therefore, 7237 is not divisible by 11.

Conclusion: After going through these steps, we found that 7237 is not divisible by any numbers other than 1 and itself, so it is a prime number. Therefore, 7237 is not a composite number.
Answer: No.

Moving on to the next prime number, 3, we sum the digits of 3833: 3 + 8 + 3 + 3 = 17. Since 17 is not divisible by 3, we can conclude that 3833 is not divisible by 3.

To determine if 5167 is a composite number, we need to check if it has any factors other than 1 and itself.

To do this, we can try dividing 5167 by all numbers from 2 to the square root of 5167 (approximately 71.8).

However, performing the division calculations for all these numbers may be time-consuming and not practically feasible. 

Instead, we can use a more efficient method called the Sieve of Eratosthenes. This method allows us to quickly determine if a number is prime or composite.

Using the Sieve of Eratosthenes:

1. Create a list of all numbers from 2 to 5167.
2. Start with the first number in the list (2) and mark it as prime.
3. Cross out all other multiples of 2 in the list (i.e., 4, 6, 8, 10, ...).
4. Move to the next unmarked number (3) and mark it as prime.
5. Cross out all other multiples of 3 in the list (i.e., 6, 9, 12, 15, ...).
6. Repeat steps 4 and 5 for the remaining unmarked numbers until you reach the square root of 5167 or the next unmarked number is greater than the square root of 5167.
7. If any numbers from 2 to the square root of 5167 remain unmarked, then 5167 is a composite number. Otherwise, if all numbers are marked, then 5167 is a prime number.

Using this method, we would find that all numbers from 2 to the square root of 5167 (approximately 71) are crossed out. Therefore, there are no remaining unmarked numbers, indicating that 5167 is a prime number.

Hence, the answer is No, 5167 is not a composite number. It is a prime number.
